GENESIS 1:1	 @ At the beginning of God’s creating<br>	of the heavens and the earth,2 	when the earth was Confusion and Chaos,<br>	darkness over the face of Ocean,<br>	rushing-spirit of God hovering over the face of the waters—3 @ 	God said: Let there be light! And there was light.4 	God saw the light: that it was good.<br>	God separated the light from the darkness.5 	God called the light: Day, and the darkness he called: Night.<br>	There was setting, there was dawning: day one.6 @ 	God said:<br>	Let there be a dome amid the waters,<br>	and let it separate waters from waters!7 	God made the dome<br>	and separated the waters that were below the dome from the waters that were above the dome.<br>	It was so.8 	God called the dome: The Heavens.<br>	There was setting, there was dawning: second day.9 @ 	God said:<br>	Let the waters under the heavens be gathered to one place,<br>	and let the dry land be seen!<br>	It was so.10 	God called the dry land: Earth, and the gathering of the waters he called: Seas.<br>	And God saw that it was good.11 	God said:<br>	Let the earth sprout forth with sprouting-growth,<br>	plants seeding forth seeds, fruit trees yielding fruit, after their kind, in which is their seed, on the earth!<br>	It was so.12 	The earth brought forth sprouting-growth,<br>	plants seeding forth seeds, after their kind,<br>	trees yielding fruit, in which is their seed, after their kind.<br>	And God saw that it was good.13 	There was setting, there was dawning: third day.14 @ 	God said:<br>	Let there be lights in the dome of the heavens, to separate the day from the night,<br>	that they may be for signs—for set-times, for days and years,15 	and let them be for lights in the dome of the heavens, to provide light upon the earth!<br>	It was so.16 	God made the two great lights,<br>	the greater light for ruling the day and the smaller light for ruling the night,<br>	and the stars.17 	God placed them in the dome of the heavens18 	to provide light upon the earth, to rule the day and the night, to separate the light from the darkness.<br>	And God saw that it was good.19 	There was setting, there was dawning: fourth day.20 @ 	God said:<br>	Let the waters swarm with a swarm of living beings, and let flying-birds fly above the earth, across the dome of the heavens!21 	So God created the great sea-serpents<br>	and all living beings that crawl about, with which the waters swarmed, after their kind,<br>	and all winged birds after their kind.<br>	And God saw that it was good.22 	And God blessed them, saying:<br>	Bear fruit and be many and fill the waters in the seas,<br>	and let the birds be many on earth!23 	There was setting, there was dawning: fifth day.24 @ 	God said:<br>	Let the earth bring forth living beings after their kind,<br>	herd-animals, crawling things, and the wildlife of the earth after their kind!<br>	It was so.25 	God made the wildlife of the earth after their kind, and the herd-animals after their kind, and all crawling things of the soil after their kind.<br>	And God saw that it was good.26 	God said:<br>	Let us make humankind, in our image, according to our likeness!<br>	They shall have dominion over the fish of the sea, the birds of the heavens, animals, all the earth, and all crawling things that crawl about on the earth!27 		So God created humankind in his image,<br>		in the image of God did he create it,<br>		male and female he created them.28 	God blessed them,<br>	and God said to them:<br>	Bear fruit and be many and fill the earth<br>	and subdue it!<br>	Have dominion over the fish of the sea, the birds of the heavens, and all living things that crawl about on the earth!29 	And God said:<br>	Here, I give you<br>	all plants seeding forth seeds that are upon the face of all the earth,<br>	and all trees in which there is tree fruit seeding forth seeds;<br>	for you shall they be, for eating,30 	and also for all the living things of the earth, for all the birds of the heavens, for all crawling about on the earth in which there is living being—<br>	all green plants for eating.<br>	It was so.31 	Now God saw all that he had made,<br>	and here, it was exceedingly good!<br>	There was setting, there was dawning: the sixth day.2:1 @ 	Thus were finished the heavens and the earth, with all of their array.2 	God had finished, on the seventh day, his work that he had made,<br>	and then he ceased, on the seventh day, from all his work that he had made.3 	God gave the seventh day his blessing, and he hallowed it,<br>	for on it he ceased from all his work, that by creating, God had made.4 	These are the begettings of the heavens and the earth: their being created.<br> @ 	At the time of <sc>Yhwh</sc> God’s making of earth and heaven,5 	no bush of the field was yet on earth,<br>	no plant of the field had yet sprung up,<br>	for <sc>Yhwh</sc> God had not made it rain upon the earth,<br>	and there was no human/<i>adam</i> to work the ground/<i>adama</i>—6 	but a surge would well up from the earth and water all the face of the ground.7 	And <sc>Yhwh</sc> God formed the human, of dust from the ground;<br>	he blew into his nostrils the breath of life<br>	and the human became a living being.8 @ 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> God planted a garden in Eden/Land-of-Pleasure, in the east,<br>	and there he placed the human whom he had formed.9 	And <sc>Yhwh</sc> God caused to spring up from the ground<br>	every type of tree, desirable to look at and good to eat,<br>	and the Tree of Life in the midst of the garden<br>	and the Tree of the Knowing of Good and Evil.10 @ 	Now a river goes out from Eden, to water the garden,<br>	and from there it divides and becomes four stream-heads.11 	The name of the first one is Pishon/Spreader—that is the one that goes around all the land of Havila, where gold is;12 	the gold of that land is good, there too are bdellium and the precious-stone carnelian.13 	The name of the second river is Gihon/Gusher—that is the one that goes around all the land of Cush.14 	The name of the third river is Hiddekel/Tigris—that is the one that goes to the east of Assyria.<br>	And the fourth river—that is Perat/Euphrates.15 @ 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> God took the human and set him in the garden of Eden,<br>	to work it and to watch it.16 	And <sc>Yhwh</sc> God commanded concerning the human, saying:<br>	From every [other] tree of the garden you may eat, yes, eat,17 	but from the Tree of the Knowing of Good and Evil—<br>	you are not to eat from it,<br>	for on the day that you eat from it, you must die, yes, die!18 @ 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> God said:<br>	It is not good for the human to be alone;<br>	I will make him a helper corresponding to him.19 	So <sc>Yhwh</sc> God formed from the ground all the wildlife of the field and all the birds of the heavens<br>	and brought [each] to the human, to see what he would call it;<br>	and whatever the human called it as a living being, that became its name.20 	The human called out names for all the herd-animals and for the birds of the heavens and for all the wildlife of the field,<br>	but for the human, there could not be found a helper corresponding to him.21 	So <sc>Yhwh</sc> God caused a deep slumber to fall upon the human, so that he slept;<br>	then he took one of his ribs and closed up the flesh in its place.22 	And <sc>Yhwh</sc> God built the rib that he had taken from the human into a woman<br>	and brought her to the human.23 	The human said:<br>		This-time, she-is-it!<br>		Bone from my bones<br>		and flesh from my flesh!<br>		She shall be called: Woman/<i>Isha,</i><br>		for from Man/<i>Ish</i> she was taken!24 	Therefore a man leaves his father and his mother and clings to his wife,<br>	and they become one flesh.25 @ 	Now the two of them, the human and his wife, were nude, yet they were not ashamed.3:1 @ 	Now the snake was more shrewd than all the living-things of the field that <sc>Yhwh</sc> God had made.<br>	It said to the woman:<br>	Even though God said: You are not to eat from any of the trees in the garden . . . !2 	The woman said to the snake:<br>	From the fruit of the [other] trees in the garden we may eat,3 	but from the fruit of the tree that is in the midst of the garden,<br>	God has said:<br>	You are not to eat from it and you are not to touch it,<br>	lest you die!4 	The snake said to the woman:<br>	Die, you will not die!5 	Rather, God knows<br>	that on the day that you eat from it, your eyes will be opened<br>	and you will become like gods, knowing good and evil.6 	The woman saw<br>	that the tree was good for eating<br>	and that it was a delight to the eyes,<br>	and the tree was desirable to contemplate.<br>	She took from its fruit and ate<br>	and gave also to her husband beside her,<br>	and he ate.7 	And the eyes of the two of them were opened<br>	and they knew [then]<br>	that they were nude.<br>	They sewed fig leaves together and made themselves loincloths.8 @ 	They heard the sound of <sc>Yhwh</sc> God [who was] walking about in the garden at the breezy-time of the day.<br>	And the human and his wife hid themselves from the face of <sc>Yhwh</sc> God, amid the trees of the garden.9 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> God called to the human and said to him:<br>	Where are you?10 	He said:<br>	I heard the sound of you in the garden and I was afraid, because I am nude,<br>	and so I hid myself.11 	He said:<br>	Who told you that you are nude?<br>	From the tree about which I commanded you not to eat,<br>	have you eaten?12 	The human said:<br>	The woman whom you gave to be beside me, she gave me from the tree,<br>	and so I ate.13 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> God said to the woman:<br>	What, now, have you done?<br>	The woman said:<br>	The snake enticed me,<br>	and so I ate.14 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> God said to the snake:<br>	Because you have done this,<br>	cursed be you from all the animals and from all the wildlife of the field;<br>	on your belly shall you walk and dust shall you eat, all the days of your life.15 	Enmity will I put between you and the woman, between your seed and her seed:<br>	they will bruise you on the head, and you will bruise them in the heel!16 	To the woman he said:<br>	I will multiply, multiply your pain [from] your pregnancy;<br>	with pains shall you bear children.<br>	Toward your husband will be your lust, yet he will rule over you.17 	To Adam he said:<br>	Because you hearkened to the voice of your wife<br>	and ate from the tree about which I commanded you, saying:<br>	You are not to eat from it!<br>	Cursed be the ground on your account;<br>	with painstaking-labor shall you eat from it, all the days of your life.18 	Thorn and sting-shrub let it spring up for you,<br>	when you [wish to] eat the plants of the field!19 	By the sweat of your nostrils shall you eat bread,<br>	until you return to the ground,<br>	for from it you were taken.<br>	For you are dust, and to dust shall you return.20 @ 	The human called his wife’s name: Havva/Life-giver,<br>	for she became the mother of all the living.21 @ 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> God made Adam and his wife coats of skins, and he clothed them.22 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> God said:<br>	Here, the human has become like one of us, in knowing good and evil.<br>	So now, lest he send forth his hand<br>	and take also from the Tree of Life<br>	and eat<br>	and live throughout the ages . . . !23 	So <sc>Yhwh</sc> God sent him away from the garden of Eden, to work the ground from which he had been taken.24 	He drove the human out<br>	and caused to dwell, east of the garden of Eden,<br>	the winged-sphinxes and the flashing, ever-turning sword<br>	to watch over the way to the Tree of Life.4:1 @ 	The human knew Havva his wife;<br>	she became pregnant and bore Kayin.<br>	She said:<br>	<i>Kaniti</i>/I-have-gotten<br>	a man, along with <sc>Yhwh</sc>!2 	And she continued bearing—his brother, Hevel.<br>	Now Hevel became a shepherd of flocks, and Kayin became a worker of the ground.3 @ 	It was, after the passing of days,<br>	that Kayin brought, from the fruit of the ground, a gift to <sc>Yhwh</sc>,4 	while as for Hevel, he too brought—from the firstborn of his flock, from their fat-parts.<br>	<sc>Yhwh</sc> had regard for Hevel and his gift,5 	but for Kayin and his gift he had no regard.<br>	Kayin became exceedingly upset and his face fell.6 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> said to Kayin:<br>	Why are you upset? Why has your face fallen?7 	Is it not [thus]:<br>	if you intend good, bear-it-aloft,<br>	but if you do not intend good,<br>	at the entrance is sin, a crouching-demon,<br>	toward you his lust—<br>	but you can rule over him.8 @ 	Kayin said to Hevel his brother . . .<br>	But then it was, when they were out in the field<br>	that Kayin rose up against Hevel his brother<br>	and he killed him.9 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> said to Kayin:<br>	Where is Hevel your brother?<br>	He said:<br>	I do not know. Am I the watcher of my brother?10 	Now he said:<br>	What have you done!<br>	A sound—your brother’s blood cries out to me from the ground!11 	And now,<br>	cursed be you from the ground,<br>	which opened up its mouth to receive your brother’s blood from your hand.12 	When you wish to work the ground<br>	it will not henceforth give its strength to you;<br>	wavering and wandering must you be on earth!13 	Kayin said to <sc>Yhwh</sc>:<br>	My iniquity is too great to be borne!14 	Here, you drive me away today from the face of the ground,<br>	and from your face I must conceal myself,<br>	I must be wavering and wandering on earth—<br>	now it will be:<br>	whoever comes upon me will kill me!15 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> said to him:<br>	No, therefore,<br>	whoever kills Kayin, sevenfold will it be avenged!<br>	So <sc>Yhwh</sc> set a sign for Kayin,<br>	so that whoever came upon him would not strike him down.16 	Kayin went out from the face of <sc>Yhwh</sc><br>	and settled in the land of Nod/Wandering, east of Eden.17 @ 	Kayin knew his wife;<br>	she became pregnant and bore Hanokh.<br>	Now he became the builder of a city<br>	and called the city’s name according to his son’s name, Hanokh.18 	To Hanokh was born Irad;<br>	Irad begot Mehuyael,<br>	Mehuyael begot Metushael,<br>	Metushael begot Lemekh.19 @ 	Lemekh took himself two wives:<br>	the name of the [first] one was Ada, the name of the second was Tzilla.20 	Ada bore Yaval&mdash;<br>	he was the father of those who sit amid tent and herd.21 	His brother’s name was Yuval&mdash;<br>	he was the father of all those who play the lyre and the pipe.22 	And Tzilla bore as well—Tuval-Kayin,<br>	burnisher of every blade of bronze and iron.<br>	Tuval-Kayin’s sister was Naama.23 @ 	Lemekh said to his wives:<br>		Ada and Tzilla, hearken to my voice,<br>		wives of Lemekh, give ear to my saying:<br>		Aye—a man I kill for wounding me,<br>		a lad for [only] bruising me!24 		Aye—if sevenfold vengeance be for Kayin,<br>		then for Lemekh, seventy-sevenfold!25 	Adam knew his wife again, and she bore a son.<br>	She called his name: Shet/Granted-One,<br>	meaning: God has granted me another seed in place of Hevel,<br>	for Kayin killed him.26 	To Shet as well a son was born;<br>	he called his name: Enosh/Mortal.<br> @ 		At that time they first called out the name of <sc>Yhwh</sc>.5:1 @	This is the record of the begettings of Adam/Humankind.<br>		At the time of God’s creating humankind,<br>		in the likeness of God did he [then] make it,2 		male and female he created them<br>		and gave blessing to them<br>		and called their name: Humankind<br>		on the day of their being created.3 	Adam lived thirty and a hundred years,<br>	and then he begot one in his likeness, according to his thirty years;<br>	then he died.6 @ 	Shet lived five years and a hundred years, and then he begot Enosh.7 	And Shet lived after he begot Enosh seven years and eight hundred years, and he begot sons and daughters.8 	Now all the days of Shet were twelve years and nine hundred years; then he died.9 @ 	Enosh lived ninety years, and then he begot Kenan.10 	And Enosh lived after he begot Kenan fifteen years and eight hundred years, and he begot sons and daughters.11 	Now all the days of Enosh were five years and nine hundred years;<br>	then he died.12 @ 	Kenan lived seventy years, and @ 	Hanokh lived sixty-five years, and then he begot Metushelah.22 	And Hanokh walked in accord with God after he begot Metushelah three hundred years, and he begot sons and daughters.23 	Now all the Metushelah were sixty-nine years and nine hundred years;<br>	then he died.28 @ 	Lemekh lived eighty-two years and a hundred years, and then he begot a son.29 	He called his name: Noah,<br>	saying:<br>	<i>Zeh yenahamenu</i>/May this-one comfort-our-sorrow<br>	from our toil, from the pains of our hands<br>	coming from the ground, which <sc>Yhwh</sc> has cursed.30 @ 	And Lemekh lived after he begot Noah ninety-five years and five hundred years, and he begot sons and daughters.31 	Now all the days of Lemekh were seventy-seven years and seven hundred years;<br>	then he died.32 @ 	Noah was five hundred years old,<br>	and then Noah begot Shem, Ham, and Yefet.6:1 @ 	Now it was when humans first became many on the face of the ground<br>	and women were born to them,2 	that the divine ones saw how fair the human women were,<br>	so they took themselves wives, whomever they chose.3 @ 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> said:<br>	My rushing-spirit shall not remain in humankind for ages, for they too are flesh;<br>	let their days be then a hundred and twenty years!4 	The giants were on earth in those days,<br>	and afterward as well,<br>	when the divine beings came in to the human women<br>	and they bore them [children]—<br>	they were the mighty-ones who were of ages [past], the men of name.5 @ 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> saw<br>	that great was humankind’s evildoing on earth<br>	and every form of their heart’s planning was only evil all the day.6 	Then <sc>Yhwh</sc> was sorry<br>	that he had made humankind on earth,<br>	and it pained his heart.7 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> said:<br>	I will blot out humankind, whom I created, from the face of the earth,<br>	from man to beast, to crawling thing and to the birds of the heavens,<br>	for I am sorry that I made them.8 	But Noah found favor in the eyes of <sc>Yhwh</sc>.9 @ 	These are the begettings of Noah.<br>	Noah was a righteous, wholehearted man in his generation;<br>	in accord with God did Noah walk.10 	And Noah begot three sons: Shem, Ham, and Yefet.11 @ 	Now the earth had gone to ruin before God, the earth was filled with wrongdoing.12 	God saw the earth, and here, it had gone to ruin,<br>	for all flesh had ruined its way upon the earth.13 @ 	God said to Noah:<br>	An end of all flesh has come before me,<br>	for the earth is filled with wrongdoing through them;<br>	here, I am about to bring ruin upon them, along with the earth.14 	Make yourself an ark of <i>gofer</i> wood;<br>	of reeds make the ark,<br>	and cover it within and without with a covering-of-pitch.15 	And this is how you are to make it:<br>	three hundred cubits the length of the ark, fifty cubits its breadth, and thirty cubits its height.16 	A skylight you are to make for the ark, and finish it to a cubit upward.<br>	The entrance of the ark you are to set in its side;<br>	with a lower, a second, and a third deck you are to make it.17 	As for me,<br>	here, I am about to bring on the Deluge, water upon the earth,<br>	to bring ruin upon all flesh that has rush of life in it, from under the heavens;<br>	all that is on earth will expire.18 	But I will establish my covenant with you:<br>	you are to come into the ark, you and your sons and your wife and your sons’ wives with you,19 	and from all living things, from all flesh, you are to bring two from all into the ark, to remain alive with you.<br>	They are to be a male and a female [each],20 	from birds after their kind, from herd-animals after their kind, from all crawling things of the ground after their kind,<br>	two from all are to come to you, to remain alive.21 	As for you,<br>	take for yourself from all edible-things that are eaten and gather it to you;<br>	it shall be for you and for them, for eating.22 	Noah did it,<br>	exactly as God commanded him, so he did.7:1 @ 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> said to Noah:<br>	Come, you and all your household, into the ark!<br>	For you I have seen as righteous before me in this generation.2 	From all [ritually] pure animals you are to take seven and seven [each], a male and his mate,<br>	and from all the animals that are not pure, two [each], a male and his mate,3 	and also from the birds of the heavens, seven and seven out all existing-things that I have made, from the face of the earth.5 	Noah did it, exactly as <sc>Yhwh</sc> had commanded him.6 @ 	Now Noah was six hundred years old when the Deluge occurred, water upon the earth;7 	and Noah came, his sons and his wife and his sons’ wives with him, into the ark before the waters of the Deluge.8 	From the pure animals and from the animals that are not pure and from the birds and all that crawls about on the ground—9 	two and two [each] came to Noah, into the ark, male and female,<br>	as God had commanded Noah.10 @ 	After the seven days it the wellsprings of the great Ocean<br>		and the sluices of the heavens opened up.12 	The torrent was upon the earth for forty days and forty nights.13 @ 	On that very day came Noah, and Shem, Ham, and Yefet, Noah’s sons, and Noah’s wife and his three sons’ wives with them, into the ark,14 	they and all wildlife after their kind, all herd-animals after their kind, all crawling things that crawl life.16 	And those that came, male and female from all flesh they came,<br>	as God had commanded him.<br>	<sc>Yhwh</sc> closed [the door] upon him.17 @ 	Now the Deluge was forty days upon the waters.19 	When the waters had swelled exceedingly, yes, exceedingly over the earth, all high mountains that were under all the heavens were covered.20 	Fifteen cubits upward swelled the waters; thus the mountains were covered.21 @ 	Then expired all flesh that crawls about upon the earth—birds, herd-animals, wildlife, and all swarming things that swarm on the earth,<br>	and all humans;22 	all that had the breath of the rush of life in their nostrils,<br>	all that were on dry-land, died.23 	He blotted out all existing-things that were on the face of the ground,<br>	from man to beast, to crawling thing and to birds of the heavens;<br>	they were blotted out from the earth.<br>	Noah alone remained, and those who were with him in the ark.24 	The waters swelled upon the earth for a hundred and fifty days.8:1 @ 	But God paid mind to Noah and all living-things, all the animals that were with him in the ark,<br>	and God brought a rushing-wind across the earth, so that the waters abated.2 	The wellsprings of Ocean and the sluices of the heavens were dammed up,<br>	and the torrent from the heavens was held back.3 	The waters returned from upon the earth, advancing and years of Avram’s being settled in the land of Canaan,<br>	and gave her to her husband Avram as a wife for him.4 	He came in to Hagar, and she became pregnant.<br>	But [when] she saw that she was pregnant, I have become of light-worth in her eyes.<br>	May <sc>Yhwh</sc> see-justice-done between me and you!6 @ 	Avram said to Sarai:<br>	Here, your maid is in your hand, deal with her however will tell you of.3 	Avraham started-early in the morning;<br>	he saddled his donkey,<br>	he took his two serving-lads with him and Yitzhak his son,<br>	he split wood for the offering-up<br>	and arose and went to the place that God had told him of.4 	On the third day Avraham lifted up his eyes<br>	and saw the place from afar.5 	Avraham said to his lads:<br>	You stay here with the donkey,<br>	and I and the lad wish to go yonder;<br>	we wish to bow down and then return to you.6 	Avraham took the wood for the offering-up,<br>	and placed them upon Yitzhak his son,<br>	while in his hand he took the fire and the knife.<br>	Thus the two of them went together.7 	Yitzhak said to Avraham his father, he said:<br>	Father!<br>	He said:<br>	Here I am, my son.<br>	He said:<br>	Here are the fire and the wood,<br>	but where is the lamb for the offering-up?8 	Avraham said:<br>	God will see-for-himself to the lamb for the offering-up,<br>	my son.<br>	Thus the two of them went together.9 	They came to the place that God had told him of;<br>	there Avraham built the altar<br>	and arranged the wood<br>	and bound Yitzhak his son<br>	and placed him on the altar atop the wood.10 	And Avraham stretched out his hand,<br>	he took the knife to slaughter his son.11 	But <sc>Yhwh’s</sc> messenger called to him from heaven<br>	and said:<br>	Avraham! Avraham!<br>	He said:<br>	Here I am.12 	He said:<br>	Do not stretch out your hand against the lad,<br>	do not do anything to him!<br>	For now I know<br>	that you are in awe of God—<br>	you have not withheld your son, your only one, from me.13 	Avraham lifted up his eyes and saw:<br>	here, a ram caught behind in the thicket by its horns!<br>	Avraham went,<br>	he took the ram<br>	and offered it up as an offering-up in place of his son.14 	Avraham called the name of that place: <sc>Yhwh</sc> Sees.<br>	As the saying is today: On <sc>Yhwh’s</sc> mountain [it] is seen.15 	Now <sc>Yhwh’s</sc> messenger called to Avraham a second time from heaven16 	and said:<br>	By myself I swear<br>	—<sc>Yhwh’s</sc> utterance—<br>	indeed, because you have done this thing, have not withheld your son, your only one,17 	indeed, I will bless you, bless you,<br>	I will make your seed many, yes, many,<br>	like the stars of the heavens and like the sand that is on the shore of the sea;<br>	your seed shall possess the gate of their enemies,18 	and all the nations of the earth shall enjoy blessing through your seed,<br>	in consequence that you hearkened to my voice!19 	Avraham returned to his lads;<br>	they arose and went together to Be’er-Sheva.<br>	And Avraham stayed in Be’er-Sheva.20 @ 	Now after these events it was, that it was told to Avraham, saying:<br>	Here, Milca too has borne, bore to Nahor, Avraham’s brother.24 	And his concubine—her name was Re’uma—bore too: Tevah, Gaham, Tahash, and Maakha.23:1 @ 	Now Sara’s life was one hundred years and twenty years and seven years, [thus] the years of Sara’s life.2 	Sara died in Arba-Town&mdash;that is Hevron, in the land of Canaan.<br>	Avraham set about to lament for Sara and to weep over her;3 	then Avraham arose from the presence of his dead<br>	and spoke to the Sons of Het, saying:4 	I am a sojourner settled among you;<br>	give me [title to] a burial holding among you,<br>	so that I may bury my dead from my presence.5 	The Sons of Het answered Avraham, saying to him:6 	Hear us, my lord!<br>	You are one exalted by God in our midst—<br>	in the choicest of our burial-sites you may bury your dead;<br>	no man among us will deny you his burial-site<br>	for burying your dead!7 	Avraham proceeded to bow low to the People of the Land, to the Sons of Het,8 	and spoke with them, saying:<br>	If it be then according to your wish<br>	that I bury my dead from my presence,<br>	hear me and interpose for me to Efron son of Tzohar,9 	that he may give me [title to] the cave of Makhpela, that is his, that is Avraham in the ears of the Sons of Het,<br>	of all who had entry to the council-gate of his city,<br>	saying:11 	Not so, my lord, hear me!<br>	The field I give to you,<br>	and the cave that is the People of the Land, saying:<br>	But if you yourself would only hear me out!<br>	I will give the silver-payment for the field;<br>	accept it from me,<br>	so that I may bury my dead there.14 	Efron answered Avraham, saying to him:15 	My lord—hear me!<br>	[A piece of] land worth four hundred silver weight,<br>	what is that between me and you!<br>	So your dead, bury!16 	Avraham hearkened to Efron:<br>	Avraham weighed out to Efron the silver-worth<br>	of which he had spoken in the hearing of the Sons of Het—<br>	four hundred silver weight at the going merchants’ rate.17 	Thus was established the field of Efron, that is in Makhpela, that faces Mamre,<br>	the field as well as the cave that is in it, and the trees that were in all the field, that were in all their territory round Het.24:1 @ 	Now Avraham was old, advanced in days,<br>	and <sc>Yhwh</sc> had blessed Avraham in everything.2 	Avraham said to his servant, the elder of his household, who ruled over all that was outside the town at the water well<br>	at sunset, at the time when the water-drawers go out,12 	and said:<br>	O <sc>Yhwh</sc>, God of my lord Avraham,<br>	pray let it happen today for me, and deal in again.17 	And the servant ran to meet her and said:<br>	Pray let me sip a little water from your pitcher!18 	She said:<br>	Drink, my lord!<br>	And in haste she let down her pitcher on her arm and drinking-trough;<br>	then she ran to the well again to draw,<br>	and drew for all his camels.21 	The man kept staring at her,<br>	[waiting] silently to find out whether <sc>Yhwh</sc> had granted weight,23 	and said:<br>	Whose daughter are you? Pray tell me!<br>	And is there perhaps in your father’s house a place for us to spend the night?24 	She said to him:<br>	I am the daughter of Betuel, son of Milca, whom she bore to Nahor.25 	And she said to him:<br>	Yes, there is straw, yes, plenty of fodder with us, [and] yes, a place to spend the night!26 	The man did homage and bowed low before <sc>Yhwh</sc>27 	and said:<br>	Blessed be <sc>Yhwh</sc>, God of my lord Avraham,<br>	who has not relinquished his loyalty and his faithfulness from my lord!<br>	While as for me, <sc>Yhwh</sc> has led me on the journey to the house of my another well, but they did not quarrel over it,<br>	so he called its name: Rehovot/Space,<br>	and said: Indeed, now <sc>Yhwh</sc> has made space for us, so that we may bear fruit in the land!23 	He 	Now Lavan had gone to shear his flock;<br>	Rahel, meanwhile, stole the <i>terafim</i> that belonged to her father.20 	Now Yaakov stole the wits of Lavan the Aramean,<br>	by not telling him that he never miscarried,<br>	the rams from your flock I never have eaten,39 	none torn-by-beasts have I ever brought you—<br>	I would make good the loss,<br>	at my hand you would seek it,<br>	stolen by day or stolen by night.40 	[Thus] I was:<br>	by day, parching-heat consumed me, and cold by night,<br>	and my sleep eluded my eyes.41 	It is twenty years for me now in your house:<br>	I have served you him:<br>	This is its interpretation:<br>	The three windings are three days—13 	in another three days<br>	Pharaoh will lift up your head<br>	and will restore you to your position<br>	so that you will flesh from off you.20 	And thus it was, on the third day,<br>	Pharaoh’s birthday,<br>	that he made a great drinkfest for all his servants,<br>	and he lifted up the head of the chief cupbearer and the Yosef had interpreted to them.23 	But the chief cupbearer did not keep Yosef in mind;<br>	he forgot him.41:1 @ 	Now at the end of two years’-time it was<br>	that Pharaoh dreamt:<br>	now here, he was standing by the Nile-Stream,2 	and here, out of the Nile, seven cows were coming up,<br>	beautiful of appearance and well-nourished of flesh,<br>	and they grazed in the reed-grass.3 	And here, seven lean of flesh ate up<br>	the seven cows beautiful in appearance, the well-nourished ones.<br>	Pharaoh awoke.5 	He fell asleep and dreamt a second time:<br>	now here, seven ears-of-grain were going up on a single stalk, fat and good,6 	and here, seven ears, lean and scorched by the east wind, were springing up after them.7 	And the lean ears swallowed up<br>	the seven well-nourished and full ears.<br>	Pharaoh awoke,<br>	and here, [it was] a dream!8 	But in the morning it was, that his spirit was stirred up,<br>	so he sent and had all of Egypt’s magicians and all of its wise-men called.<br>	Pharaoh recounted his dream to them,<br>	but no one could interpret them to Pharaoh.9 	Then the chief cupbearer spoke up to Pharaoh, saying:<br>	I must call my faults to mind today!10 	Pharaoh sent and had Yosef called.<br>	They quickly brought him out of the pit;<br>	he shaved, changed his clothes, and came before Pharaoh.15 	Pharaoh said to Yosef:<br>	I have dreamt a dream, and there is no interpreter for it!<br>	But I have heard it said of you<br>	that you [but] need to hear a dream in order to interpret it!16 	Yosef answered Pharaoh, saying:<br>	Not I!<br>	God will answer what is for Pharaoh’s welfare.17 	Pharaoh spoke to Yosef:<br>	In my dream—<br>	here, I was standing on the bank of the Nile,18 	and here, out of the Nile were coming up seven lank of flesh,<br>	in all the land of Egypt I have never seen their like for ill-condition!20 	Then the seven lank and ill-looking cows ate up<br>	the first seven cows, the well-nourished ones.21 	They entered their innards, but you would not know that they had entered their innards, for they were as ill-looking as at the beginning!<br>	And I awoke.22 	Then I saw in my dream:<br>	now here, seven ears were going up on a single stalk, full and good,23 	and here, seven ears, hardened, lean, and scorched by the east wind, were springing up after them.24 	Then the lean ears swallowed up<br>	the seven good ears!<br>	Now I have spoken with the magicians, but there is no one that can tell me [the answer]!25 	Yosef said to Pharaoh:<br>	Pharaoh’s dream is one.<br>	What God is about to do, he has told Pharaoh.26 	The seven good cows<br>	are seven years,<br>	and the seven good ears<br>	are seven years;<br>	the dream is one.27 	And the seven lank and ill-looking cows that were coming up after them<br>	are seven years,<br>	and the seven ears, hollow and scorched by the east wind,<br>	will be seven years of famine!28 	That is the word that I spoke to Pharaoh:<br>	what God is about to do, he has let Pharaoh see.29 	Here,<br>	seven years are coming<br>	of great plenty in all the land of Egypt.30 	But seven years of famine will arise after them,<br>	when all the plenty in the land of Egypt will be forgotten.<br>	The famine will destroy the land,31 	and it will not be known, that plenty [that was] in the land,<br>	because of that famine afterward,<br>	for it will be exceedingly heavy.32 	Now as for the repetition of the dream to Pharaoh, twice over: [it means] that the matter is determined by God,<br>	and God is hastening to do it.33 	So-now, let Pharaoh select a discerning and wise man,<br>	and set him over the land of Egypt.34 	Let Pharaoh do [this]: let him appoint appointed-overseers for the land,<br>	and divide the land of Egypt into five parts during the seven years of plenty.35 	Let them collect all kinds of food from these good years that are coming,<br>	and let them pile up grain under Pharaoh’s hand as food- provisions in the cities, and keep it under guard.36 	So the provisions will be an appointed-reserve for the land<br>	for the seven years of famine that will occur in the land of Egypt,<br>	so that the land will not be cut off by the famine.37 	The words seemed good in Pharaoh’s eyes and in the eyes of all his servants,38 	and Pharaoh said to his servants:<br>	Could we find another like him, a man in whom is the spirit of a god?39 	Pharaoh said to Yosef:<br>	Since a god has made you know all this,<br>	there is none as wise and discerning as you;40 	you shall be [The One] Over My House!<br>	To your orders shall all my people submit;<br>	only by the throne will I be greater than you!41 	And Pharaoh said to Yosef:<br>	See, I place you over all the land of Egypt!42 	And Pharaoh removed his signet-ring from his hand and placed it on Yosef’s hand,<br>	and he had him clothed in linen garments and put the gold chain upon his neck;43 	he had him mount the chariot of his second-in-rank, and they called out before him: <i>Avrekh!</i>/Attention!<br>	Thus he placed him over all the land of Egypt.44 	Pharaoh said to Yosef:<br>	I am Pharaoh,<br>	but without you, no man shall raise hand or foot in all the land of Egypt!45 	And Pharaoh called Yosef’s name: <i>Tzafenat Pane’ah</i>/The God Speaks and He Lives,<br>	and he gave him Asenat, daughter of Poti Fera, priest of On, as a wife.<br>	And Yosef’s [influence] went out over the land of Egypt.46 	Now Yosef was thirty years old when he stood in the presence of Pharaoh, king of Egypt.<br>	And Yosef went out from Pharaoh’s presence and crossed through all the land of Egypt.47 @ 	In the seven years of plenty the land produced in handfuls.48 	And he collected all kinds of provisions from those seven years that occurred in the land of Egypt,<br>	and placed provisions in the towns.<br>	The provisions from the fields of a town, surrounding it, he placed in it [as well].49 	So Yosef piled up grain like the sand of the sea, exceedingly much, until they had to stop counting, for it was uncountable.50 @ 	Now two sons were born to Yosef, before the year of famine came,<br>	whom Asenat, daughter of Poti Fera, priest of On, bore to him.51 	Yosef called the name of the firstborn: Menashe/He-Who-Makes-Forget,<br>	meaning: God has made-me-forget all my hardships, all my father’s house.52 	And the name of the second he called: Efrayim/Double-Fruit,<br>	meaning: God has made me bear fruit in the land of my affliction.53 @ 	There came to an end the seven years of plenty that had occurred in the land of Egypt,54 	and there started to come the seven years of famine, as Yosef had said.<br>	Famine occurred in all lands, but in all the land of Egypt there was bread.55 	Then all the land of Egypt felt the famine, and the rations, to Yosef,<br>	for the famine was strong in all lands.42:1 @ 	Yaakov saw that there were rations in Egypt,<br>	so Yaakov said to his sons:<br>	Why do you keep looking at one another?2 	And he said:<br>	Here, I have heard that there are rations in Egypt;<br>	go down there and buy us rations from there,<br>	that we may live and not die.3 	So Yosef’s brothers went down, ten [of little-ark of papyrus,<br>	she loamed it with loam and with pitch,<br>	and placed the child in it,<br>	and placed it in the reeds by the shore of the Nile.4 	And his sister stationed herself far off, <i>meshitihu</i>/I-pulled-him.11 @ 	Now it was some years later, Moshe grew up;<br>	he went out to his brothers and saw their burdens.<br>	And he saw an Egyptian man striking a Hebrew man, [one] of Pharaoh and before the eyes of his servants,<br>	and all the water that was in the Nile changed into blood.21 	The fish that were in the Nile died, and the Nile reeked,<br>	and the Egyptians could not drink water from the Nile;<br>	the blood was throughout all the land of Egypt.22 	But the magicians of Egypt did thus with their occult-arts,<br>	and Pharaoh’s heart remained strong-willed, and he did not hearken to them,<br>	as <sc>Yhwh</sc> had spoken.23 	So Pharaoh faced about and came into his house; neither did he pay any mind to this.24 	But all Egypt had to dig around the Nile to drink water,<br>	for they could not drink from the waters of the Nile.25 	Seven days were fulfilled, after <sc>Yhwh</sc> had struck the Nile.26 @ 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> said to Moshe:<br>	Come to Pharaoh and say to him:<br>	Thus says <sc>Yhwh</sc>:<br>	Send free my people, that they may serve me!27 	Now if you refuse to send them free,<br>	here, I will smite your entire territory with frogs.28 	The Nile will swarm with frogs;<br>	they will ascend, they will come<br>	into your house, into your bedroom, upon your couch,<br>	into your servants’ houses, in among your people,<br>	into your ovens and into your dough-pans&mdash;29 	onto you, onto your people, onto all your servants will the frogs ascend!8:1 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> said to Moshe:<br>	Say to Aharon:<br>	Stretch out your hand with your frog-horde ascended<br>	and covered the land of Egypt.3 	Now the magicians did thus with their occult-arts:<br>	they made frogs ascend upon the land of Egypt.4 	Pharaoh had Moshe and Aharon called<br>	and said:<br>	Plead with <sc>Yhwh</sc>, that he may remove the frogs from me and from my people,<br>	and I will send the people free, that they may sacrifice to <sc>Yhwh</sc>!5 	Moshe said to Pharaoh:<br>	Be praised over me:<br>	For when shall I plead for you, for your servants, for your people,<br>	to cut off the frogs from you and from your houses,<br>	[so that] only in the Nile will they remain?6 	He said:<br>	For the morrow.<br>	He said:<br>	According to your words, [then]!<br>	In order that you may know<br>	that there is none like <sc>Yhwh</sc> our God.7 	The frogs shall remove from you, from your houses, from your servants, from your people;<br>	only in the Nile shall they remain.8 	Moshe and Aharon went out from Pharaoh,<br>	and Moshe cried out to <sc>Yhwh</sc><br>	on account of the frogs that he had imposed upon Pharaoh.9 	And <sc>Yhwh</sc> did according to Moshe’s words:<br>	the frogs died away, from the houses, from the courtyards, and from the fields.10 	They piled them up, heaps upon heaps, and the land reeked.11 	But Pharaoh saw that there was breathing-room,<br>	so he made his heart heavy-with-stubbornness, and did not hearken to them,<br>	as <sc>Yhwh</sc> had spoken.12 @ 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> said to Moshe:<br>	Say to Aharon:<br>	Stretch out your staff and strike the dust of the earth;<br>	it will become gnats throughout all the land of Egypt!13 	They did thus;<br>	Aharon stretched out his hand with his staff and struck the dust of the earth,<br>	and gnats were on man and on beast;<br>	all the dust of the earth became gnats throughout all the land of Egypt.14 	Now the magicians did thus with their occult-arts, to bring forth the gnats, but they could not,<br>	and the gnats were on man and on beast.15 	The magicians said to Pharaoh:<br>	This is the finger of a god!<br>	But Pharaoh’s heart remained strong-willed, and he did not hearken to them,<br>	as <sc>Yhwh</sc> had spoken.16 @ 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> said to Moshe:<br>	Start-early in the morning, station yourself before Pharaoh—here, he goes out to the water&mdash;<br>	and say to him:<br>	Thus says <sc>Yhwh</sc>:<br>	Send free my people, that they may serve me!17 	Indeed, if you do not send my people free,<br>	here, I will send upon you, upon your servants, upon your people, upon your houses—<br>	an insect-swarm,<br>	the houses of Egypt will be full of the insects,<br>	as well as the ground upon which they are!18 	But I will make distinct, on that day, the region of Goshen, where my people is situated,<br>	so that there will be no insects there,<br>	in order that you may know that I am <sc>Yhwh</sc> in the land.19 	And I will put a ransom between my people and your people—<br>	on the morrow will this sign occur.20 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> did thus:<br>	heavy insect-swarms came into Pharaoh’s house, into the houses of his servants, throughout all the land of Egypt;<br>	the land was in ruins in the face of the insects.21 	Pharaoh had Moshe and Aharon called<br>	and said:<br>	Go, sacrifice to your god in the land!22 	Moshe said:<br>	It would not be wise to do thuswise:<br>	for Egypt’s abomination is what we sacrifice to our God;<br>	if we were to sacrifice Egypt’s abomination before their eyes,<br>	would they not stone us?23 	Let us go a three days’ journey into the wilderness,<br>	and we shall sacrifice to <sc>Yhwh</sc> our God, as he has said to us.24 	Pharaoh said:<br>	I will send you free,<br>	that you may sacrifice to <sc>Yhwh</sc> your God in the wilderness;<br>	only: you are not to go far, too far!<br>	Plead for me!25 	Moshe said:<br>	Here, when I go out from you, I will plead with <sc>Yhwh</sc>,<br>	and the insects will remove from Pharaoh, from his servants, and from his people, on the morrow,<br>	only: let not Pharaoh continue to deal-wantonly [with us],<br>	by not sending the people free to sacrifice to <sc>Yhwh</sc>!26 	Moshe went out from before Pharaoh and pleaded with <sc>Yhwh</sc>.27 	And <sc>Yhwh</sc> did according to Moshe’s words,<br>	he removed the insects from Pharaoh, from his servants and from his people&mdash;<br>	not one remained.28 	But Pharaoh made his heart heavy-with-stubbornness this time as well,<br>	and he did not send the people free.9:1 @ 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> said to Moshe:<br>	Come to Pharaoh and speak to him:<br>	Thus says <sc>Yhwh</sc>, the God of the Hebrews:<br>	Send free my people, that they may serve me!2 	If you refuse to send [them] free, and continue to hold-on-strongly to them,3 	here, <sc>Yhwh’s</sc> hand will be on your livestock in the field,<br>	on the horses, on the donkeys, on the camels, on the oxen, and on the sheep—<br>	an exceedingly heavy pestilence!4 	And <sc>Yhwh</sc> will make-a-distinction between the livestock of Israel and the livestock of Egypt:<br>	there will not die among all that belong to the Children of Israel a thing!5 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> set an appointed-time, saying:<br>	On the morrow, <sc>Yhwh</sc> will do this thing in the land.6 	And <sc>Yhwh</sc> did that thing on the morrow—<br>	all the livestock of Egypt died,<br>	but of the livestock of the Children of Israel, there died not one.7 	Pharaoh sent [to inquire], and here: there had not died of the livestock of the Children of Israel even one.<br>	But Pharaoh’s heart remained heavy-with-stubbornness, and he did not send the people free.8 @ 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> said to Moshe and to Aharon:<br>	Take yourselves fistfuls of soot from a furnace<br>	and let Moshe toss it heavenward before Pharaoh’s eyes;9 	it will become fine-dust on all the land of Egypt,<br>	and on man and on beast, it will become boils sprouting into blisters,<br>	throughout all the land of Egypt!10 	They took the soot from a furnace and stood before Pharaoh, and Moshe tossed it heavenward,<br>	and it became boil blisters, sprouting on man and on beast.11 	Now the magicians could not stand before Moshe because of the boils,<br>	for the boils were upon the magicians and upon all Egypt.12 	But <sc>Yhwh</sc> made Pharaoh’s heart strong-willed, and he did not hearken to them,<br>	as <sc>Yhwh</sc> had said to Moshe.13 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> said to Moshe:<br>	Start-early in the morning, station yourself before Pharaoh and say to him:<br>	Thus says <sc>Yhwh</sc>, the God of the Hebrews:<br>	Send free my people, that they may serve me!14 	Indeed, this time I will send all my blows upon your heart, and against your servants, and against your people,<br>	so that you may know that there is none like me throughout all the land;15 	indeed, by now I could have sent out my hand and struck you and your people with the pestilence,<br>	and you would have been effaced from the land;16 	however, just on account of this I have allowed you to withstand,<br>	to make you see my power.<br>	and in order that they might recount my name throughout all the land.17 	[But] still you set yourself up over my people, by not sending them free—18 	here, around this time tomorrow I will cause to rain down an exceedingly heavy hail,<br>	the like of which has never been in Egypt from the days of its founding until now!19 	So-now:<br>	send [word]: give refuge to your livestock and to all that is yours in the field;<br>	all men and beasts who are found in the field and who have not been gathered into the house—<br>	the hail will come down upon them, and they will die!20 	Whoever had awe for the word of <sc>Yhwh</sc> among Pharaoh’s servants had his servants and his livestock flee into the houses,21 	but whoever did not pay any mind to the word of <sc>Yhwh</sc> left his servants and his livestock out in the field.22 @ 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> said to Moshe:<br>	Stretch out your hand toward the heavens,<br>	and let there be hail throughout all the land of Egypt,<br>	on man and on beast and on all the plants of the field, throughout the land of Egypt!23 	Moshe stretched out his staff toward the heavens,<br>	and <sc>Yhwh</sc> gave forth thunder-sounds and hail, and fire went toward the earth,<br>	and <sc>Yhwh</sc> caused hail to rain down upon the land of Egypt.24 	There was hail and a fire taking-hold-of-itself amidst the hail, exceedingly heavy,<br>	the like of which had never been throughout all the land of Egypt since it had become a nation.25 	The hail struck, throughout all the land of Egypt, all that was in the field, from man to beast;<br>	all the plants of the field the hail struck, and all the trees of the field it broke down;26 	only in the region of Goshen, where the Children of Israel were, was there no hail.27 	Pharaoh sent and had Moshe and Aharon called<br>	and said to them:<br>	This-time I have sinned!<br>	<sc>Yhwh</sc> is the one-in-the-right, I and my people are the ones-in-the-wrong!28 	Plead with <sc>Yhwh</sc>,<br>	for too much is the God-thunder and this hail!<br>	Let me send you free—do not continue staying here!29 	Moshe said to him:<br>	As soon as I have gone out of the city, I will spread out my hands to <sc>Yhwh</sc>;<br>	the thunder will stop and the hail will be no more—<br>	in order that you may know that the land belongs to <sc>Yhwh</sc>.30 	But as for you and your servants,<br>	I know well that you do not yet stand-in-fear<br>	before the face of <sc>Yhwh</sc> God!31 	—Now the flax and the barley were stricken, for the barley was in ears and the flax was in buds,32 	but the wheat and the spelt were not stricken, for they are late-ripening.—33 	Moshe went from Pharaoh, outside the city, and spread out his hands to <sc>Yhwh</sc>,<br>	and the thunder and the hail stopped, and the rain no longer poured down to earth.34 	Pharaoh saw that the rain and the hail and the thunder had stopped,<br>	so he continued to sin: he made his heart heavy-with-stubbornness, his and his servants’.35 	Pharaoh’s heart remained strong-willed, and he did not send the Children of Israel free,<br>	as <sc>Yhwh</sc> had spoken through Moshe.10:1 @ 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> said to Moshe:<br>	Come to Pharaoh!<br>	For I have made his heart and the heart of his servants heavy-with-stubbornness,<br>	in order that I may put these my signs among them2 	and in order that you may recount in the hearing God!<br>	Do you not yet know that Egypt is lost?8 	Moshe and Aharon were returned to Pharaoh,<br>	and he said to them:<br>	Go, serve <sc>Yhwh</sc> your God!<br>	—Who is it, who is it that would go?9 	Moshe said:<br>	With our young ones, with our elders we will go,<br>	with our sons and with our daughters,<br>	with our sheep and with our oxen we will go—<br>	for it is <sc>Yhwh’s</sc> pilgrimage-festival for us.10 	He said to them:<br>	May <sc>Yhwh</sc> be thus with you, the same as I mean to send you free along with your little-ones!<br>	You see—yes, your faces are set toward ill!11 	Not thus—go now, O males, and serve <sc>Yhwh</sc>, for <i>that<i> is what you seek!<br>	And they were driven out from Pharaoh’s face.12 @ 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> said to Moshe:<br>	Stretch out your left;<br>	nothing at all green was left of the trees and of the plants of the field, throughout all the land of Egypt.16 	Quickly Pharaoh had Moshe and Aharon called<br>	and said:<br>	I have sinned against <sc>Yhwh</sc> your God and against you!17 	So now,<br>	pray bear my sin just this one time!<br>	And plead with <sc>Yhwh</sc> your God,<br>	that he may only remove this death from me!18 	He locust remained throughout all the territory of Egypt.20 	But <sc>Yhwh</sc> made Pharaoh’s heart strong-willed, and he did not send the Children of Israel free.21 @ 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> said to Children of Israel, there was light in their settlements.24 	Pharaoh had Moshe called and said:<br>	Go, serve <sc>Yhwh</sc>;<br>	only your sheep and your oxen shall be kept back&mdash;<br>	even your <sc>Yhwh</sc> made Pharaoh’s heart strong-willed, so that he would not consent to send them free.28 	Pharaoh said to him:<br>	Go from me!<br>	Take you care:<br>	You are not to see my face again,<br>	for on the day that you see my face, you shall die!29 	Moshe said:<br>	You have spoken well;<br>	I will not henceforth see your face again!11:1 @ 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> said to Moshe:<br>	I will many in the land of Egypt.10 	Now Moshe and Aharon had done all the portents in Pharaoh’s presence,<br>	but <sc>Yhwh</sc> had made Pharaoh’s heart strong-willed, and he had not sent the Children of Israel free from his land.12:1 @ 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> said to Moshe and to Aharon in the land of Egypt, saying:2 	Let this month be for you the beginning of months,<br>	the beginning-one let it be for you of the months of the year.3 	Speak to the entire community of Israel, saying:<br>	On the tenth day of this month<br>	they are to take them, each-man, a lamb, according to their Fathers’ House, a lamb per household.4 	Now if there be too few in the house for a lamb,<br>	he is to take [it], he and his neighbor who is near his house, by the computation according to the [number of] persons;<br>	each-man according to what he can eat you are to compute for the lamb.5 	A wholly-sound male, year-old lamb shall be yours; from the sheep and from the goats are you to take it.6 	It shall be for you in safekeeping, until the fourteenth day of this month,<br>	and they are to slaughter it—the entire assembly of the community of Israel—between the setting-times.7 	They are to take some of the blood and put it onto the two posts and onto the lintel,<br>	onto the houses in which they eat it.8 	And they are to eat the flesh on that night, roasted in fire,<br>	and <i>matzot;</i><br>	with bitter-herbs they are to eat it.9 	Do not eat any of it raw, or boiled, boiled in water,<br>	but rather roasted in fire, its head along with its legs, along with its innards.10 	You are not to leave any of it until morning;<br>	what is left of it until morning, with fire you are to burn.11 	And thus you are to eat it:<br>	your hips girded, your sandals on your feet, and your sticks in your hand.<br>	And you are to eat it in trepidation—<br>	it is a Passover-Meal to <sc>Yhwh</sc>.12 	I will proceed through the land of Egypt on this night<br>	and will strike down every firstborn in the land of Egypt, from man to beast,<br>	while on all the gods of Egypt I will render judgment,<br>	I, <sc>Yhwh!</sc>.13 	Now the blood will be a sign for you upon the houses where you are:<br>	I will see the blood, and I will pass over you,<br>	so that the blow will not become a bringer-of-ruin to you, when I strike down the land of Egypt.14 	Now this day shall be a reminder for you;<br>	you are to celebrate it as a pilgrimage-celebration for <sc>Yhwh</sc>;<br>	throughout your generations, as a law for the ages you are to celebrate it!15 	For seven days, <i>matzot</i> you are to eat;<br>	already on the first day you are to get rid of leaven from your houses,<br>	for anyone who eats what is fermented—from the first day until the seventh day—: that person shall be cut off from Israel!16 	And on the first day, a proclamation of holiness,<br>	and on the seventh day, a proclamation of holiness shall there be for you&mdash;<br>	no kind of work is to be made on them;<br>	only what belongs to every person to eat, that alone may be made-ready by you.17 	And keep the [Festival of] <i>Matzot!</i><br>	For on this same day<br>	I have brought out your forces from the land of Egypt.<br>	Keep this day throughout your generations as a law for the ages.18 	In the first [month], on the fourteenth day of the month, at sunset, you are to eat <i>matzot,</i><br>	until the twenty-first day of the month, at sunset.19 	For seven days, no leaven is to be found in your houses,<br>	for whoever eats what ferments, that person shall be cut off from the community of Israel,<br>	whether sojourner or native of the land.20 	Anything that ferments you are not to eat;<br>	in all your settlements, you are to eat <i>matzot.</i>21 	Moshe had all the elders of Israel called and said to them:<br>	Pick out, take yourselves a sheep for your clans, and slaughter the Passover-animal.22 	Then take a band of hyssop, dip [it] in the blood which is in the basin,<br>	and touch the lintel and the two posts with some of the blood which is in the basin.<br>	Now you—you are not to go out, any man from the entrance to his house, until daybreak.23 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> will proceed to deal-blows to Egypt,<br>	and [when] he sees the blood on the lintel and on the two posts, <br>	<sc>Yhwh</sc> will pass over the entrance,<br>	and will not give the ruinbringer [leave] to come into your houses to deal-the-blow.24 	You are to keep this matter<br>	as a law for you and for your children, into the ages!25 	Now it will be,<br>	when you come to the land which <sc>Yhwh</sc> will give you, as he has promised,<br>	you are to keep this service!26 	And it will be,<br>	when your children say to you: What does this service [mean] to you?27 	then say:<br>	It is the sacrificial-meal of Passover to <sc>Yhwh</sc>,<br>	who passed over the houses of the Children of Israel in Egypt,<br>	when he dealt-the-blow to Egypt and our houses he rescued.<br>	The people did homage and bowed low.28 	And the Children of Israel went and did [it];<br>	as <sc>Yhwh</sc> had commanded Moshe and Aharon, thus they did.29 @ 	Now it was in the middle of the night:<br>	<sc>Yhwh</sc> struck down every firstborn in the land of Egypt,<br>	from the firstborn of Pharaoh who sits on his throne<br>	to the firstborn of the captive in the dungeon,<br>	and every firstborn of beast.30 	Pharaoh arose at night,<br>	he and all his servants and all Egypt,<br>	and there was a great cry in Egypt,<br>	for there was not a house in which there was not one this-side and one on this-side.<br>	So his hands remained steadfast, until the sun came in.13 	And Yehoshua weakened Amalek and his people, with the edge of the sword.14 	<sc>Yhwh</sc> said to Moshe:<br>	Write this as a memorial in a record<br>	and put it in Yehoshua’s hearing:<br>	Yes, I will wipe out, wipe out the memory of Amalek from under the heavens!15 	Moshe built an altar<br>	and 	You will become worn out, yes, worn out, so you, so this people that are with you,<br>	for this matter is too heavy for you;<br>	you cannot do it alone.19 	So now, hearken to my voice:<br>	I will advise you, so that God may be with you:<br>	Be, yourself, for the people in relation to God.<br>	You yourself should have the matters come to God;20 	You should make clear to them the laws and the God in awe,<br>	men of truth, hating gain;<br>	you should set [them] over them<br>	as chiefs of thousands, chiefs of hundreds, chiefs of fifties, and chiefs of tens,22 	so that they may render chiefs of hundreds, chiefs of fifties, and chiefs of tens.26 	They would render judgment for the people at all times:<br>	the difficult matters they would bring before Moshe,<br>	but every small matter they would judge by themselves.27 	Moshe sent his father-in-law off,<br>	and he went home to his land.19:1 @ 	In the third month after the going-out of the Children of Israel from the land of opposite the mountain.3 	Now Moshe went up to God,<br>	and <sc>Yhwh</sc> called out to him from the mountain,<br>	saying:<br>	Say thus to the House of Yaakov,<br>	[yes,] tell the Children of nakedness not be laid-bare upon it.21:1 @ 	Now these are the regulations that you are to set before them:2 	When you acquire a Hebrew serf,<br>	for six years he is to serve,<br>	but in the seventh he is to go out at liberty, for nothing.3 	If he came by himself, he is to go out by himself;<br>	if he was the spouse of a wife, his wife is to go out with him.4 	If his lord gives him a wife, and she bore him sons or daughters,<br>	the wife and those she bore are to remain her lord’s, and he is to go out by himself.5 	But if the serf should say, yes, say:<br>	I love my lord, my wife and my designated her for himself,<br>	he is to have her redeemed;<br>	to a foreign people he has not the power to sell her,<br>	since he has betrayed her.9 	But if it is for his son that he designates her,<br>	according to the just-rights of women he is to deal with her.10 	If another he takes for himself,<br>	[then] her board, her clothing, or her oil he is not to diminish.11 	If these three he does not do for her,<br>	she is to go out for nothing, with no silver.12 @ 	He that strikes a man, so that he dies,<br>	is to be put to death, yes, death.13 	Now should he not have lain in wait [for 	When men quarrel, and a man strikes his neighbor with a stone or with a fist, yet he does not die, but rather takes to his bed:19 	if he can rise and walk about outside upon his crutch,<br>	he that struck [him] is to go clear;<br>	only: he is to make good for his resting-time, and provide-that-he-be-healed, yes, healed.20 @ 	When a man strikes his serf or his handmaid with a rod, so that he [only] according to assessment.23 	But if harm should occur,<br>	then you are to give life in place of life—24 	eye in place of eye, tooth in place of tooth, hand in place of25 	hand, foot in place him free at liberty [on account of] his eye;27 	if the tooth of his serf or the tooth of his handmaid he breaks off,<br>	he is to send him free at liberty [on account of] his tooth.28 @ 	When an ox gores a man or a woman, so that one dies,<br>	the ox is to be stoned, yes, stoned, and its flesh is not to be eaten,<br>	and the owner of the ox is to be clear.29 	But if the ox was a gorer from yesterday [and the] day-before, and it was so designated to its owner,<br>	and he did not guard it,<br>	and it causes the death of a man or of a woman,<br>	the ox is to be stoned, and its owner as well is to be put to death.30 	If a ransom is established for him,<br>	he is to give it as a redemption for his life, all that is imposed for him.31 	Whether it is a son it gores or a daughter it stoned.33 @ 	When a man opens up a pit, or when a man digs a pit, and does not cover it up, and an ox or a donkey falls into it,34 	the owner of the pit is to pay, the worth-in-silver he is to restore to its owner, and the dead-animal is to remain his.35 	When a man’s ox deals-a-blow to his neighbor’s ox, so that it dies,<br>	they are to sell the live ox and split its worth-in-silver, [and you brings near a near-offering for <sc>Yhwh</sc><br>	from domestic-animals: from the herd or from the flock you may bring near your near-offering.3 	If an offering-up is his near-offering, from the herd,<br>	male, wholly-sound, let him bring it near;<br>	to the entrance of the Tent of Appointment let him bring it near,<br>	as acceptance for him, before the presence of <sc>Yhwh</sc>.4 	He is to lean his hand on the head of the offering-up,<br>	that there may be acceptance on his behalf, to effect-ransom for him.5 	He is to slaughter the herd-animal [for sacrifice] before the presence of <sc>Yhwh</sc>,<br>	and the Sons of Aharon, the priests, are to bring near the blood<br>	and are to dash the blood against the altar, all around,<br>	that is at the entrance of the Tent of Appointment.6 	Then he is to flay the offering-up, and is to section it into its sections.7 	Now the Sons of Aharon the priest are to put fire on the altar<br>	and are to arrange wood on the fire.8 	The Sons of Aharon, the priests, are to arrange the sections, the head and the suet,<br>	on the wood that is on the fire, that is on the altar,9 	while its innards and its shins he is to wash in water;<br>	and the priest is to turn all-of-it into smoke upon the altar,<br>	for an offering-up, a fire-offering of soothing savor for <sc>Yhwh</sc>.10 @ 	Now if from the flock is his near-offering,<br>	from the sheep or from the goats, for an offering-up,<br>	male, wholly-sound, let him bring it near.11 	He is to slaughter it on the flank of the altar, northward, before the presence of <sc>Yhwh</sc>,<br>	and the Sons of Aharon, the priests, are to dash its blood against the altar, all around.12 	Then he is to section it into its sections, with its head and with its near and turn it into smoke upon the altar:<br>	it is an offering-up,<br>	a fire-offering of soothing savor for <sc>Yhwh</sc>.14 	Now if from birds is his offered-up near-offering for <sc>Yhwh</sc>,<br>	he is to bring near from turtledoves or from young pigeons as his near-offering.15 	The priest is to bring it near on the altar<br>	and pinch off its head;<br>	he is to turn it into smoke on the altar,<br>	and its blood is to be drained out against the side-wall of the altar.16 	He is to remove its crissum by means of its plumage<br>	and is to fling it next to the altar, eastward,<br>	into the place of the ashes.17 	He is to tear it open by its wings—he is not to divide [it]!—<br>	and the priest is to turn it into smoke upon the altar, on the wood that is on the fire:<br>	it is an offering-up,<br>	a fire-offering of soothing savor for <sc>Yhwh</sc>.2:1 @ 	Now a person—when he brings near a near-offering of a grain-gift for <sc>Yhwh</sc>,<br>	of [proper] flour shall his near-offering be.<br>	He is to pour oil on it and is to put frankincense on it;2 	then he is to bring it to the Sons of Aharon, the priests.<br>	He is to scoop from there a scoopful from its flour and from its oil, along with all its frankincense;<br>	the priest is to turn its reminder-portion into smoke upon the altar,<br>	a fire-offering of soothing savor for <sc>Yhwh</sc>.3 	Now what is left of the grain-gift is Aharon’s and his sons’,<br>	a holiest holy-portion from the fire-offerings of <sc>Yhwh</sc>.4 @ 	When you bring near a near-offering of a grain-gift baked in an oil—unleavened shall it be.6 	Crumble it into crumbled-bits, and pour oil on it;<br>	it is a grain-gift.7 	And if a grain-gift in a frying-pan is your near-offering,<br>	of flour in oil shall it be Aharon’s and his sons’,<br>	a holiest holy-portion from the fire-offerings of <sc>Yhwh</sc>.11 	Every grain-gift that you bring near to <sc>Yhwh</sc>&mdash;it is not to be made leavened,<br>	for any the reminder-portion into smoke, from its grits and from its oil, along with all its frankincense,<br>	as a fire-offering for <sc>Yhwh</sc>.3:1 @ 	Now if a sacrifice of <i>shalom</i> is his your generations, throughout all your settlements:<br>	any fat and any blood you are not to eat!4:1 @ 	Now <sc>Yhwh</sc> spoke to Moshe, saying:2 	Speak to the Children of Israel, saying:<br>	[Any] animals—<br>	that-one you may eat.4 	However, these you are not to eat<br>	from those bringing up the cud, or from those having a hoof:<br>	the camel, for it brings up the cud, but a hoof it does not have,<br>	it is <i>tamei</i> for you;5 	the hyrax, for it brings up the cud, but a hoof it does not have,<br>	it is <i>tamei</i> for you;6 	the hare, for it brings up the cud, but a hoof it does not have,<br>	it is <i>tamei</i> for you;7 	the pig, for it has a hoof and cleaves a cleft in the hoof, but [as for] it—the cud it does not chew up,<br>	it is <i>tamei</i> for you.8 	From their flesh you are not to eat, their carcasses you are not to touch,<br>	they are <i>tamei</i> for you!9 @ 	These you may eat from all that are in the water:<br>	any one that has fins and scales in the water, [whether] in the seas or in the streams,<br>	them you may eat.10 	But any one that does not have fins and scales,<br>	[whether] in the seas or in the streams,<br>	from all swarming-things in the water, from all living beings that are in the water—<br>	they are detestable-things for you!11 	And they shall remain detestable-things for you:<br>	from their flesh you are not to eat, their owl, the screech owl and the sea gull,<br>	and the falcon after its kind;17 	the little-owl, the cormorant, and the great owl;18 	the barn-owl, the pelican, and the Egyptian-vulture;19 	the stork, <i>tamei</i> for you,<br>	whoever touches them is <i>tamei!</i>27 	And any one that goes about on its paws, among all animals that go about on all fours,<br>	they are <i>tamei</i> for monitor and the lizard,<br>	the sand-lizard and the chameleon.31 	These are the ones <i>tamei</i> for you among all the swarming-creatures;<br>	whoever touches them when they are dead shall be can be used in work—<br>	it is to be put through water;<br>	it remains-<i>tamei</i> until sunset,<br>	and then it is pure.33 	And [regarding] any earthen vessel into which one of them falls, within touches their carcass shall be <i>tamei</i>.37 	Now if [part] of their carcass falls upon any sowing seed that is to be sown,<br>	it remains-pure.38 	But if water is put on the seed and [part] of their carcass falls on it,<br>	it is <i>tamei</i> for you.39 	If there should die one of the animals that are [permitted] to you for eating,<br>	one who touches its carcass shall remain-<i>tamei</i> remain-<i>tamei</i> until sunset.41 @ 	Any swarming-creature that swarms upon the earth:<br>	it is a detestable-thing, it is not to be eaten.42 	Anything going about on its belly, anything going
